Master's Ownership of Ma'dhun's Earnings When Debt Overwhelms
Intra-Hanafi dispute on master's rights to ma'dhun's earnings when debt overwhelms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether the master owns the earnings of an authorized slave when debt overwhelms, and apply the condition of freedom from need to determine ownership.

Core Idea
Master's ownership of the slave's earnings is conditioned on the property being free from the slave's need; overwhelming debt blocks it.

The authorized slave (ma'dhun) trades with the master's permission, but what happens when his debts exceed his assets? This lesson unpacks a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn over who owns the slave's earnings. Understanding the condition of 'freedom from need' is key to navigating this issue and its practical consequences for sales, gifts, and manumission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Recognize that the dispute centers on whether the master's ownership of the ma'dhun's earnings is absolute or conditional. The trigger is when the slave's debt surrounds (yuhitu) his entire property and physical person (raqabah).
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Imam holds the master does not own the earnings. His proof: ownership requires the property to be free from the slave's need (farigh 'an hajatih). Overwhelming debt makes the property occupied (mashghul) by need, thus no ownership.
This is a rational argument (dalil 'aqli) based on the purpose of ownership.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold the master owns the earnings. Their proof: ownership of the slave's person (raqabah) is the cause for ownership of earnings. Overwhelming debt does not remove the slave from the master's ownership, analogized to the permissibility of intercourse with a female ma'dhuna.
They use qiyas (analogy) to a stronger case.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and thamarah
Imam distinguishes between ownership of the person and ownership of earnings. The condition for the latter is freedom from need, which is absent. The practical difference appears in sales, gifts, and manumission: according to Imam, the master's dispositions are void; according to Sahibayn, they are valid but he must guarantee the debt.
The author of Bahr al-Raiq sides with Imam's view as the relied-upon position.
5
Explore the subsidiary rulings
The text extends the dispute to manumission (it is void according to Imam, effective according to Sahibayn but with guarantee), and to buying a mahram relative (freed only according to Sahibayn). Also, distinctions are made between due and deferred debts.
These applications clarify the scope of the ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (ولا يملك سيده ما في يده لو أحاط دينه بما في يده ورقبته وهذا عند الإمام. وقالا : يملك ذلك لأن ملك الرقبة سبب الملك كسب اليد واستغراقها بالدين لا يوجب خروج المأذون عن ملكه ولهذا ملك وطء المأذونة فكذا كسبه الذي في يده لأنه يتبع أصله فيكون مثله. ولأبي حنيفة أن ملك المولى أنما يثبت في ملك العبد التاجر عند فراغه عن حاجته والمحيط خلافه عند مشغول بحاجته فلا يملك. قال في العناية : الدين لا يخلو إما أن يحيط بماله ورقبته أو لا يحيط أو أحاط بماله دون رقبته أو برقبته دون ماله وأطلق في دين العبد فشمل ما إذا كان حالاً أو مؤجلاً. وفي العتابية : ولو باع المولى المأذون أو كسبه والدين مؤجل جاز ويضمن إذا حل الأجل. وفي المحيط : عبد عليه دين إلى أجل فباعه مولاه جاز ونفذ لأن العبد ما به حق الغريم ولا منفعة فإذا حل الأجل ضمن المولى قيمته. وفيه أيضاً ولا يجوز هبة مال عبده المأذون المديون وإن أجازه الغرماء لأنه تعلق الدين بماليته ولو وهب عبده المأذون المديون ذكر في بعض الروايات أنه لا يجوز، وفي بعضها يجوز، قيل ما ذكر أنه يجوز محمول على ما إذا لم يقض المولى دينه أو لم تبره الغرماء. وفيه أيضاً : وهب عبده المأذون المديون من رجل وعليه ألف حالة وألف مؤجلة فلصاحب الحال أن ينقض البيع في الكل ولو عيب الموهوب له العبد ضمن المولى لرب الدين نصف قيمته. وظاهر قوله ولصاحب الحال النقض وما قبله أن الدين إذا كان مؤجلاً ملك المولى ولو كان الدين مستغرقاً ولو قيد به لكان أولى . قال رحمه الله : ( وبطل تحريره عبداً من كسبه) وهذا عند الأمام ولما كان العتق أقوى من غيره صرح به ليفيد أن تصرف المولى في غيره باطل بالطريق الأولى. وعندهما ينفذ عتقه وهو نظير المكاتب فإن المولى يملك رقبته حتى يعتق بإعتاقه ولا يملك ما في يده من لا ينفذ إعتاقه فيه فإذا نفذ عتقه في رقبته المأذون له عنده وعندهما فيه وفي كسبه يضمن للغرماء قيمته لأنه أتلف بالإعتاق ما تعلق به حقهم وكذا لو أتلف المولى ما في يده من العبيد بالقتل يضمن لما ذكرنا لكن يضمن قيمته للحال عندهما لأنه ملكه لتعلق كسب العبد كذلك وعندهما ينفذ ويضمن حق الغير به، وعنده في ثلاث سنين لأنه ضمان حياته لعدم ملكه. ولو اشترى ذا رحم محرم من المولى لم يعتق عنده لعدم الملك، وعندهما يعتق،
He (the author), may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'And his master does not own what is in his hand if his debt surrounds what is in his hand and his physical person' – this is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He owns that, because ownership of the physical person is a cause for ownership of the earnings of the hand, and its being overwhelmed by debt does not necessitate the slave's removal from his ownership, and therefore he is allowed to have intercourse with the female authorized slave, and similarly his earnings that are in his hand, because it follows its origin, so it is like it. According to Abu Hanifa, the master's ownership is only established in the property of the trading slave when it is free from his need, while the opposite is the case when it is occupied with his need, so he does not own it. The author of Al-Inayah said: The debt is either such that it surrounds his wealth and his physical person, or does not surround, or surrounds his wealth without his physical person, or his physical person without his wealth. And he spoke in absolute terms about the slave's debt, so it includes whether it is due or deferred. In Al-'Itabiyyah: If the master sells the authorized slave or his earnings while the debt is deferred, it is permissible, and he is liable when the term matures. In Al-Muhit: A slave who owes a debt deferred to a term, and his master sells him, it is permissible and effective, because the slave has no benefit from the creditor's right. When the term matures, the master guarantees his value. Also in it: It is not permissible to gift the property of his indebted authorized slave, even if the creditors consent, because the debt is attached to its monetary value. And if the master gifts his indebted authorized slave, it is mentioned in some narrations that it is not permissible, and in some it is permissible. It is said that what is mentioned as permissible is interpreted as the case where the master does not repay his debt or the creditors do not release him. Also in it: He gifted his indebted authorized slave to a man, and the slave owed a thousand due and a thousand deferred. Then the owner of the due debt has the right to rescind the sale in its entirety. And if the donee found a defect in the slave, the master guarantees to the creditor half of his value. The apparent meaning of his statement 'the owner of the due debt has the right to rescind' and what precedes it is that if the debt is deferred, the master owns it, even if the debt is overwhelming. If he had qualified it, it would have been better. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'And his freeing a slave from his earnings is void' – this is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. Since manumission is stronger than other dispositions, he mentioned it to indicate that other dispositions of the master are invalid by even stronger reason. According to the two, his manumission is effective. It is analogous to the mukatab (slave under contract of manumission): the master owns his physical person such that he becomes free if the master frees him, but he does not own what is in his hand of that which his manumission is not effective. So if his manumission is effective in the physical person of the authorized slave according to him, while according to the two it is effective in both, then the master guarantees to the creditors its value because he destroyed by manumission what their rights were attached to. Similarly, if the master destroys what is in his hand of slaves by killing, he guarantees as we mentioned, but he guarantees its value immediately according to the two because he owns it due to the attachment of the slave's earnings like that. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, he guarantees in three years because it is a guarantee of his life due to lack of ownership. And if the master buys a mahram relative (of the slave) from him, it is not freed according to Imam Abu Hanifa due to lack of ownership; according to the two, it is freed.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the master's ownership of the authorized slave's earnings when the slave's debts are overwhelming (surrounding both his wealth and his physical person). The author cites the matn stating that the master does not own the earnings according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that ownership of the slave's person is the cause for ownership of his earnings; overwhelming debt does not remove the slave from the master's ownership, analogously to the permissibility of sexual relations. Imam Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that the master's ownership is conditional on the property being free from the slave's need; the overwhelming debt constitutes a need, thus the master does not own it. The passage then provides further rulings from Al-Inayah, Al-'Itabiyyah, and Al-Muhit about selling or gifting the slave when debts are deferred. Following this, the author discusses the invalidity of the master freeing a slave from the earnings of the Ma'dhun, again with the same ikhtilaf. According to Imam, such manumission is invalid; according to the Sahibayn, it is effective but the master must guarantee the value to the creditors. The difference affects the timing of the guarantee (immediate vs. over three years). The passage concludes with the case of buying a mahram relative, where only the Sahibayn consider it valid and result in emancipation.

Key Terms
الإحاطة بالدين (al-ihatah bi-al-dayn): The debt surrounds (overwhelms) the slave's entire property and physical person, meaning the debt equals or exceeds his total assets including his market value.
الرقبة (al-raqabah): The physical person of the slave, distinct from his earnings.
الكسب (al-kasb): Earnings acquired through the slave's trade or labor.
المأذون (al-ma'dhun): A slave authorized by his master to engage in trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The master owns them absolutely.
B) The master does not own them.
C) The master owns them but must give half to creditors.
D) The matter is unresolved.

Key Takeaway
The master's ownership of the ma'dhun's earnings is contingent on the slave's property being free from need; overwhelming debt severs this ownership according to Imam Abu Hanifa.

Master's Ownership of Slave's Earnings When Debt Encompasses
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the master's ownership of a ma'dhun slave's earnings when debt is encompassing, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and distinguish the conditions for ownership.

Core Idea
The master does not own the slave's earnings when the slave's debt encompasses his value and possessions—the slave's need takes priority.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ownership of earnings acquired by a ma'dhun (trading) slave when his debts consume all his assets and his personal value. The author, Ibn Nujaym, states the matn (core ruling) that the master does not own such earnings according to Imam Abu Hanifa, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree. Understanding this ruling requires careful consideration of the condition of 'freedom from need' (farigh an hajatihi) and the analogy (qiyas) based on milk al-raqaba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the matn: the author states that the master does not own what is in the slave's hand if debt encompasses both his hand-possessions and his person (his price). Note that this is attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa.
The phrase 'ولا يملك سيده ما في يده' is the decisive ruling.
2
Examine the opponents' proof (qiyas)
The two companions argue that ownership of the slave's person (milk al-raqaba) is a cause for ownership of anything attached to the slave, like earnings. They analogize from the right to cohabit (milk al-wat') which remains despite debt.
Their qiyas is based on the principle 'al-kasb yatba' al-asl' (earnings follow origin).
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's counter-argument
Abu Hanifa introduces the condition of being free from need (farigh an hajatihi). When the slave's property is occupied by debt (need), the master's ownership does not vest. The debt is a right of others that takes priority.
This condition is not explicit in the Sahibayn's reasoning, making it a point of ikhtilaf.
4
Apply the categories of debt
The commentary from al-'Inaya categorizes debt as encompassing assets and person, only assets, only person, or none. The ruling varies accordingly. Understand that only encompassing debt triggers Abu Hanifa's view.
The passage also discusses selling/gifting the slave, showing practical implications.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
Though the text does not explicitly declare the preferred view, the structure and later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Hidayah) prefer Abu Hanifa's position. The master does not own the earnings when debt is encompassing.
This is the operative fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (ولا يملك سيده ما في يده لو أحاط دينه بما في يده ورقبته وهذا عند الإمام. وقالا : يملك ذلك لأن ملك الرقبة سبب الملك كسب اليد واستغراقها بالدين لا يوجب خروج المأذون عن ملكه ولهذا ملك وطء المأذونة فكذا كسبه الذي في يده لأنه يتبع أصله فيكون مثله. ولأبي حنيفة أن ملك المولى أنما يثبت في ملك العبد التاجر عند فراغه عن حاجته والمحيط خلافه عند مشغول بحاجته فلا يملك. قال في العناية : الدين لا يخلو إما أن يحيط بماله ورقبته أو لا يحيط أو أحاط بماله دون رقبته أو برقبته دون ماله وأطلق في دين العبد فشمل ما إذا كان حالاً أو مؤجلاً. وفي العتابية : ولو باع المولى المأذون أو كسبه والدين مؤجل جاز ويضمن إذا حل الأجل. وفي المحيط : عبد عليه دين إلى أجل فباعه مولاه جاز ونفذ لأن العبد ما به حق الغريم ولا منفعة فإذا حل الأجل ضمن المولى قيمته. وفيه أيضاً ولا يجوز هبة مال عبده المأذون المديون وإن أجازه الغرماء لأنه تعلق الدين بماليته ولو وهب عبده المأذون المديون ذكر في بعض الروايات أنه لا يجوز، وفي بعضها يجوز، قيل ما ذكر أنه يجوز محمول على ما إذا لم يقض المولى دينه أو لم تبره الغرماء. وفيه أيضاً : وهب عبده المأذون المديون من رجل وعليه ألف حالة وألف مؤجلة فلصاحب الحال أن ينقض البيع في الكل ولو عيب الموهوب له العبد ضمن المولى لرب الدين نصف قيمته. وظاهر قوله ولصاحب الحال النقض وما قبله أن الدين إذا كان مؤجلاً ملك المولى ولو كان الدين مستغرقاً ولو قيد به لكان أولى.
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And his master does not own what is in his hand if his debt encompasses what is in his hand and his person. And this is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He does own that because ownership of the neck (the slave's person) is a cause for ownership, like the gain of the hand, and its being encompassed by debt does not necessitate the removal of the ma'dhun from his ownership. For this reason, he owns the right to cohabit with the female ma'dhun. So too, the earnings that are in his hand because it follows its origin and thus is like it. And for Abu Hanifa, the master's ownership is only established in the property of the trading slave when it is free from his need. The encompassing (debt) is contrary to this; when it is occupied by his need, he does not own. He said in al-'Inaya: The debt is either encompassing his property and his neck, or not encompassing, or encompassed his property but not his neck, or encompassed his neck but not his property. And he spoke absolutely regarding the slave's debt, so it includes whether it is due now or deferred. And in al-'Utabiyya: If the master sold the ma'dhun or his earnings and the debt is deferred, it is valid and he guarantees when the term comes. And in al-Muhit: A slave with a debt due at a term, if his master sells him, it is valid and executed because the slave does not have a right for the creditor and no benefit, so when the term comes, the master guarantees his value. Also in it: It is not permissible to gift the property of his ma'dhun slave who is in debt, even if the creditors allow it, because the debt is attached to his property. If he gifted his ma'dhun slave who is in debt, it is mentioned in some narrations that it is not permissible, and in some that it is permissible. It is said that what is mentioned as permissible is interpreted as the case when the master did not pay his debt or the creditors did not release him. Also in it: He gifted his ma'dhun slave who is in debt to a man, and he owed a thousand due and a thousand deferred. The creditor of the due amount has the right to rescind the sale in its entirety, and if the donee finds a defect in the slave, the master guarantees to the debt holder half his value. The apparent meaning of his statement 'the creditor of the due amount has the right to rescind' and what preceded it is that if the debt is deferred, the master owns, even if the debt was encompassing. And if it were restricted by that, it would be more appropriate.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states that the master does not own what is in the slave's hand if the slave's debt encompasses both his hand-possessions and his person (his value). This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree. They reason: The master's ownership of the slave's person (milk al-raqaba) is a cause for ownership, just as the slave's acquisition is a cause. The debt encompassing these does not remove the slave from the master's ownership. Therefore, the master still owns the slave's earnings. The commentary then presents Abu Hanifa's argument: The master's ownership over the trading slave's property is conditional on the slave being free from need (farigh an hajatihi). When the slave is burdened by debt, his property is occupied by his need, so the master does not own it. The author then quotes al-'Inaya which categorizes the relationship between debt and assets. The passage further discusses practical rulings: selling the slave when debt is deferred, gifting the slave's property, and selling the slave by the master. These all illustrate the consequences of whether the master owns the slave's earnings. According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi), when debt is encompassing, the master does not own the earnings, as per Abu Hanifa's view.

Key Terms
المأذون (al-ma'dhūn): A slave whom his master has authorized (idhn) to engage in trade. The permission grants the slave the capacity to contract and acquire property, but the master remains the owner of the slave's person.
الدين المستغرق (al-dayn al-mustaghriq): Debt that encompasses (covers) the entire value of the slave's assets and his personal value (his price). It leaves nothing for the master to own from the slave's earnings.
ملك الرقبة (milk al-raqaba): Ownership of the slave's person (the neck). This is the master's fundamental right over the slave, which includes ownership of the slave's body and its usufruct.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When the slave's debt is less than his assets
B) When the slave's debt encompasses his assets and his person
C) When the slave's debt is deferred
D) When the master has not authorized the slave to trade

Key Takeaway
The master's ownership of a ma'dhun slave's earnings is conditional on the slave being free from need; encompassing debt blocks that ownership.

Invalidity of Master's Freeing a Slave from Slave's Earnings When Debt Encompasses
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a master freeing a slave from the ma'dhun slave's earnings when debt encompasses, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and apply the rule to new scenarios.

Core Idea
The master does not own the ma'dhun's earnings when debt encompasses; thus his freeing of a slave from those earnings is invalid.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in Hanafi fiqh regarding the validity of a master's act of freeing a slave using the earnings of his ma'dhun (permitted) slave who is burdened with encompassing debt. The matn states that such a freeing is invalid according to Abu Hanifa, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold it is valid. The commentary explains the reasoning and provides examples to illustrate the practical implications. Understanding this dispute requires grasping the concept of ownership of earnings and creditors' rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exact ruling
The matn says 'وبطل تحريره عبداً من كسبه' meaning 'His freeing of a slave from his earnings is invalid.' Note that this is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa.
2
Understand the reasoning
The master does not own the earnings because the slave's debt encompasses his assets and person. Creditors have a prior right. Emancipation requires ownership of the thing freed.
3
Contrast with the two companions
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the freeing is valid but the master must compensate the creditors. They consider the master to own the earnings, but with creditors' rights attached.
4
Apply the analogy
The master's position is analogous to his relation with a mukatab (slave under kitaba): he owns the person but not the earnings that are beyond his control.
5
Derive the practical consequence
If the master frees the slave, he must pay the creditors the value of the slave, immediately per the companions, over three years per Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (وبطل تحريره عبداً من كسبه) وهذا عند الأمام ولما كان العتق أقوى من غيره صرح به ليفيد أن تصرف المولى في غيره باطل بالطريق الأولى. وعندهما ينفذ عتقه وهو نظير المكاتب فإن المولى يملك رقبته حتى يعتق بإعتاقه ولا يملك ما في يده من لا ينفذ إعتاقه فيه فإذا نفذ عتقه في رقبته المأذون له عنده وعندهما فيه وفي كسبه يضمن للغرماء قيمته لأنه أتلف بالإعتاق ما تعلق به حقهم وكذا لو أتلف المولى ما في يده من العبيد بالقتل يضمن لما ذكرنا لكن يضمن قيمته للحال عندهما لأنه ملكه لتعلق كسب العبد كذلك وعندهما ينفذ ويضمن حق الغير به، وعنده في ثلاث سنين لأنه ضمان حياته لعدم ملكه. ولو اشترى ذا رحم محرم من المولى لم يعتق عنده لعدم الملك، وعندهما يعتق، ولو استولد جارية عبده المأذون له وعليه دين مستغرق وصارت أم ولد له ويضمن قيمتها ولا يضمن عرقها ولا قيمة ولدها وهذا بإنفاق لأن عندهما ملكه ثابت حقيقة وعنده صادف حق الملك ولهذا يجوز للمولى أن يتزوجها ولو أعتقها المولى وعلى العبد دين مستغرق ثم وطئها فولدت عتقت بالاستيلاد وعليه العقر لها ويثبت نسب الولد منه عند أبي حنيفة لأن العتق توقف عنده على أن ينفذ عند تملك الجارية ألا ترى أنه لو قضى دين الغرماء أو أبرأ الغرماء العبد من ديونهم حتى ملك الجارية نفذ عتقه فكذا إذا ملك الجارية بالاستيلاد. ولو تزوج جارية عبده المأذون المديون لا يجوز؛ ذكره في المحيط. وذكر المولى مثال فإن العبد المأذون المديون إذا باعه المولى من غير إذن الغرماء وأعتقه المشتري قبل قبضه ينفذ عتقه إن أجاز الغرماء البيع أو قضى المولى دين الغرماء، وإن أبرأ الغرماء العبد عن الدين ينفذ عتق المشتري، فإن أبى الغرماء أن يجيزوا البيع والمولى لم يقض دينه فإنه يبطل عتقه ويباع العبد للغرماء بدينهم هكذا ذكر في الأصل مطلقاً. وهذا الجواب الذي قالوا لا يشكل على قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، أما على قول محمد رحمه الله تعالى فمنهم من قال لا يقف عتق المشتري على قول محمد، ومنهم من قال ما ذكر قولهم جميعاً وعلى قول محمد يحتاج إلى الفرق هذا وبين المشتري من الغاصب وهذا إذا أعتق المشتري قبل القبل، وأما إذا قبض العبد بين ثم أعتقه فإنه ينفذ عتقه، وإذا تقدم عتق المشتري بعد القبض فالغرماء بعد هذا بالخيار إن شاءوا أجاز البيع وأخذوا الثمن، وإن شاءوا ضمنوه القيمة هذا إذا أجازوا بيع المولى، وإن ضمنوا قيمته للمولى فبيع المولى ينفذ ويسلم الثمن للمولى ولو كان المشتري باع العبد بعد ما قبضه أو وهبه وقبضه الموهوب له ثم حضر الغرماء وأجازوا بيع المولى ينفذ بيع المشتري وهبته من غيره. ولو قال المؤلف فيتوقف تحريره لكان أولى لأن غايته تصرف فضولي. وقد أفاد في المحيط في مسألة الأمة المستولدة أنه موقوف فالعتق كذلك
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And his freeing of a slave from his earnings is invalid). This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And since emancipation is stronger than other acts, he specified it to indicate that the master's disposal in other things is invalid by a more primary route. According to the two, his emancipation is executed. And it is analogous to the mukatab: the master owns his person so that he can be freed by his emancipation, but he does not own what is in his hand of that in which his emancipation is not executed. So if his emancipation is executed in the person of the ma'dhun according to him and according to the two, then regarding his earnings, he guarantees their value to the creditors because he destroyed by the emancipation what their right was attached to. Similarly, if the master destroyed what was in his hand of the slaves by killing, he guarantees as we mentioned, but he guarantees its value immediately according to the two because it is his ownership due to the attachment of the slave's earnings similarly; and according to the two it is executed and he guarantees the right of others by it, and according to him in three years because it is a guarantee of his life due to lack of ownership. And if he bought a close relative (dhi rahim mahram) from the master, it is not freed according to him due to lack of ownership, and according to the two it is freed. And if he made a female slave of his ma'dhun slave pregnant (istawlada) while he had encompassing debt, and she became an umm walad for him, he guarantees her value, but he does not guarantee her offspring (عرقها) nor the value of her child. This is agreed because according to the two, his ownership is established in reality, and according to him, it met the right of ownership, and for this reason it is permissible for the master to marry her. And if the master freed her while the slave had encompassing debt, then he had intercourse with her and she gave birth, she becomes free by istilad, and he owes her 'aqr (compensation for intercourse), and the lineage of the child is established from him according to Abu Hanifa because the emancipation is suspended according to him to be executed when he owns the slave girl. Do you not see that if he paid the creditors' debt or the creditors released the slave from their debts until he owned the slave girl, his emancipation would be executed? Similarly, when he owns the slave girl by istilad. And if he married the slave girl of his ma'dhun slave who is in debt, it is not permissible; mentioned in al-Muhit. And he mentioned an example: if the ma'dhun slave who is in debt is sold by the master without the permission of the creditors, and the buyer frees him before taking possession, his emancipation is executed if the creditors validate the sale or the master pays the creditors' debt; and if the creditors release the slave from the debt, the buyer's emancipation is executed. If the creditors refuse to validate the sale and the master did not pay his debt, then his emancipation is invalid and the slave is sold for the creditors for their debt. This is how it is mentioned in al-Asl absolutely. And this answer they gave is not problematic according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. As for according to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, some said that the buyer's emancipation does not depend on his view, and some said that what is mentioned is their view collectively, and according to Muhammad, a distinction is needed between this and the buyer from a usurper. And this is if the buyer freed before taking possession. As for if he took possession of the slave and then freed him, then his emancipation is executed. And if the buyer's freedom preceded after taking possession, then the creditors after this have a choice: if they wish, they validate the sale and take the price; if they wish, they guarantee the value. This is if they validate the master's sale. And if they guarantee the value to the master, then the master's sale is executed and the price goes to the master. Even if the buyer sold the slave after taking possession or gifted him and the donee took possession, then the creditors come and validate the master's sale, the buyer's sale and gift are executed. And if the author had said 'his freeing is suspended' it would be more appropriate because its ultimate result is the disposal of a fuduli. And it is mentioned in al-Muhit regarding the issue of the umm walad that it is suspended, so emancipation is likewise.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states that the master's freeing of a slave (from the slave's earnings) is invalid. This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the emancipation is executed. The commentary explains that since emancipation is the strongest disposal, if it is invalid, then other disposals are invalid by a stronger reason. The analogy to the mukatab is drawn: the master owns the slave's person, but not what is in his hand that is beyond the master's control. If the master frees the slave, he compensates the creditors for the value of the slave because he destroyed their right. The compensation is immediate according to the two companions (as they consider the earnings owned by the master), but according to Abu Hanifa, it is spread over three years because the master does not own the earnings immediately. The passage then discusses various scenarios: buying a close relative from the master (it does not free according to Abu Hanifa), istilad (begetting a child) of the slave's female slave, and the consequences of selling the slave and the buyer freeing him before or after possession. These illustrate the implications of the dispute. The relied-upon position is that the freeing is invalid when debt is encompassing, as per Abu Hanifa, because the master does not own the earnings.

Key Terms
العتق (al-'itq): Emancipation or freeing of a slave. In this passage, it refers to the master's act of freeing a slave owned by his ma'dhun slave, using the ma'dhun's earnings.
المكاتب (al-mukātab): A slave who has entered into a contract of kitaba with his master, whereby the slave pays a sum in installments and becomes free upon payment. Analogous to the ma'dhun in that the master owns the slave's person but has limited rights over his earnings.
الغرماء (al-ghuramā'): Creditors to whom the slave is indebted. Their rights attach to the slave's assets and person, affecting the master's ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a master tries to free a slave from the earnings of his ma'dhun slave who has encompassing debt, what is the ruling?
A) The freeing is valid but the master must pay the creditors
B) The freeing is invalid because the master does not own the earnings
C) The freeing is suspended until the debt is paid
D) The slave becomes free automatically

Key Takeaway
The master's freeing of a slave from the ma'dhun's earnings is invalid when debt encompasses because the master does not own those earnings; creditors' rights take priority.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Validity of Freeing When Debt Does Not Encompass
Explaining that the master's freeing of a slave from the slave's earnings is valid if the debt does not encompass

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a master's freeing of a slave from the slave's earnings is valid according to the Hanafi mufta bihi position, and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this issue.

Core Idea
A master can free a slave from the slave's earnings only if debt does not encompass the slave's assets and person.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a specific scenario in the chapter of sales (buyu'): a master has permitted his slave to trade (ma'dhun), and the slave incurs debt while also earning. Can the master free a slave (perhaps a sub-slave) from those earnings? The matn gives a concise condition: if the debt does not encompass (lam yuhit), the freeing is valid. The commentary unpacks this by discussing the different opinions of the Hanafi imams, particularly Abu Hanifa's two positions, and affirms the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
Locate the central hukm: the master's freeing of a slave from the ma'dhun's earnings is valid (sahih) when the debt does not encompass both the slave's person (value) and his assets. Note that 'encompass' means the debt equals or exceeds the total value.
The condition is phrased as 'lam yahit' (does not encompass). The commentary explains 'ilm yahit bi-raqabati wa bi-ma fi yadih'.
2
Map the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Distinguish Abu Hanifa's first opinion (qawl al-awwal) from his second opinion (qawl al-akhar). In the first, any debt – even a small one – prevents the master from owning the earnings, so freeing is invalid. In the second, ownership depends on whether the debt encompasses the slave's assets; if not, the master owns the surplus.
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) agree with the second opinion. The first opinion is likened to a pledge (rahn) where no distinction is made between small and large debts.
3
Analyse the dalil (evidence) for the second opinion
The second opinion's reasoning is that the slave's assets are partly free (farigh) and partly occupied (mashghul). Since the condition that prevents ownership (debt encompassing) is absent, the master's ownership of the surplus is valid. This is supported by the fact that the debt attaches proportionally, not to every part equally.
This is a ta'lil (rationally derived ruling) based on the nature of ownership and debt attachment.
4
Confirm the mufta bihi position
The commentary states that the second opinion is the accepted view (mufta bihi), and it is supported by al-Hidaya and al-'Inaya. The first opinion is considered marjuh (weak) and not practised.
This is an example of how a later ruling (qawl al-akhar) can override an earlier one within the same madhhab.
5
Apply to a concrete example
Consider a ma'dhun slave with assets worth 1000 dirhams and a debt of 800 dirhams. The debt does not encompass, so the master owns the 200 dirham surplus and can free another slave from it. If the debt were 1200, it would encompass, and the freeing would be invalid.
This matches the example from al-Jami' al-Saghir mentioned at the end of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (وإن لم يحط صح) يعني وإن لم يحط الدين برقبته وبما في يده جاز عتقه وهذا بالإجماع، أما عندهما فظاهر وكذا عنده في قوله الآخر، وفي قوله الأول لا يملك فلا إعتاقه لأن الدين يتعلق يصح بكسبه وفي حق التعلق لا فرق بين القليل والكثير كما في الرهن. ووجه قول الآخر أن الفراغ وبعضه فارغ وبعضه مشغول فلا يجوز أن : الملك الحال لأن شرط يمنع في الملك لم يوجد ولا يجوز أن يمنع بقدره لأن البعض ليس بأولى من البعض الآخر؛ كذا نقله الشارح. وفي الهداية : وإن لم يكن محيطاً بماله جاز عتقه ولم يذكر رقبته وهذا هو القسم الأقسام التي ذكرناها قال في العناية : وإذا لم يكن محيطاً بماله ورقبته جاز عتق من المولى عبداً من كسبه. قال في بيوع الجامع الصغير عن يعقوب في رجل أذن لعبده في التجارة فاشترى عبداً يساوي ألفاً وعلى الأول ألف دين فأعتق المولى العبد المشتري فعتقه الشرط هو عدم الثالث
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if it does not encompass, it is valid). Meaning, if the debt does not encompass his person and what is in his hand, his freeing is valid, and this is by consensus. As for according to the two, it is apparent, and similarly according to him in his other opinion. In his first opinion, he does not own, so there is no freeing because the debt attaches to his earnings, and in terms of attachment, there is no difference between little and much, as in the case of a pledge. And the justification of the other opinion is that the slave is free from need, and some of it is free and some is occupied, so it is not permissible that the present ownership [be blocked] because the condition that prevents ownership does not exist, and it is not permissible to prevent it by its extent because one part is not more entitled than another. Thus the commentator transmitted. And in al-Hidaya: And if it is not encompassing his property, his freeing is valid, and it did not mention his person, and this is the third of the divisions we mentioned. He said in al-'Inaya: And if it is not encompassing his property and his person, the freeing by the master of a slave from his earnings is valid. He said in the sales (buyu') of al-Jami' al-Saghir from Ya'qub regarding a man who permitted his slave to trade, then he bought a slave worth a thousand while the first had a thousand dinars [of debt], then the master freed the purchased slave, [so] his freeing [is valid, and] the condition is the absence of the third [i.e., the debt not being encompassing?].
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The matn states that if the debt does not encompass, the freeing is valid. The commentary clarifies that 'not encompassing' means the debt does not cover both the slave's person (value) and his possessions. According to the two companions, this is straightforward; according to Abu Hanifa's second opinion (qawl al-akhar), it is also valid. In his first opinion (qawl al-awwal), he held that the master does not own the earnings even if the debt is small, because the attachment of debt to earnings affects all of it. But the relied-upon and mufta bihi position is the second opinion: if the debt is not encompassing, the master owns the earnings and his freeing is valid. The commentary from al-Hidaya specifies that the condition is that the debt does not encompass the slave's property (ma'l), without mentioning the person, but the author of al-‘Inaya adds that it should not encompass both property and person. The example from al-Jami' al-Saghir illustrates: a man permitted his slave to trade, the slave bought another slave worth 1000 while having a debt of 1000 (so the debt equals the new slave's value, but does it encompass the slave's total assets? Possibly the example is where the debt is not encompassing the slave's overall wealth). The passage affirms that the condition for validity is that the debt does not encompass (the third condition, i.e., the debt not being encompassing).

Key Terms
الإجماع (al-ijmā'): Consensus. Here it refers to the agreement among the Hanafi imams that when the debt does not encompass, the freeing is valid. Note: this is internal Hanafi ijmā', not necessarily the consensus of all scholars.
القول الأول (al-qawl al-awwal): The first opinion of Abu Hanifa, which held that the master never owns the slave's earnings when any debt exists, even if small, because the debt attaches to all earnings equally.
القول الآخر (al-qawl al-ākhar): The second (other) opinion of Abu Hanifa, which makes the master's ownership dependent on whether the debt encompasses the slave's assets and person. If not, the master owns the surplus and can free slaves from it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position, under what condition is the master's freeing of a slave from the ma'dhun's earnings valid?
A) Only if the slave has no debt at all
B) If the debt does not encompass the slave's entire assets and person
C) Only if the master has the permission of the creditors
D) If the slave is not a ma'dhun

Key Takeaway
A master can validly free a slave from a ma'dhun's earnings only when the debt is less than the slave's total assets and person; otherwise, the earnings are fully encumbered and the freeing is invalid.

Condition of Debt for Valid Emancipation of the Authorized Slave
Commentary on condition of debt for valid emancipation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which the emancipation of an authorized slave is valid according to Abu Hanifa's later position and explain why his first position differed.

Core Idea
Emancipation is valid only if debt does not completely encumber the slave's person and earnings.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute about the authorized slave's capacity to own and the effect of debt on his emancipation. The text presents Abu Hanifa's earlier view that the slave owns nothing, making emancipation impossible if any debt exists, and his later view, shared by the Sahibayn, that partial vacancy allows valid emancipation. Understanding this shift is essential for applying the correct fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
Find the statement in the Arabic: 'وإن لم يحط صح' meaning 'if it does not encompass, it is valid.' Determine what 'it' refers to (debt) and what must not be encompassed (person and earnings).
2
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Notice that the text mentions 'عند أبي حنيفة في قوله الآخر' (according to Abu Hanifa's other saying). Compare his first position (slave does not own) with the later position (slave can own partially). Identify the basis of each: the first analogizes debt attachment to a pledge (رهن); the later relies on partial vacancy.
The first position is abandoned; the later is mufta bihi.
3
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider the practical consequence: if debt encompasses all, emancipation is void according to the first position, but according to the later, it is either valid (if debt does not encompass) or suspended (if it does). Understand that 'sahih' here means 'nafidh' (executed).
The commentary clarifies that 'sahih' in this context means 'nafidh'.
4
Apply to the istilad example
The text applies the principle to the case where the master makes the slave's female concubine umm walad. Note how the ruling changes depending on whether debt is encompassing or not. Observe the analogy to the slave's ownership through istilad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المأذون من كسبه وإن لم يحط صح ولم يصح بيعه من السيد إلا بمثل القيمة وإن باع سيده منه ولو استولد جارية عبده المأذون له وعليه دين مستغرق وصارت أم ولد له ويضمن قيمتها ولا يضمن عرقها ولا قيمة ولدها وهذا بإنفاق لأن عندهما ملكه ثابت حقيقة وعنده صادف حق الملك ولهذا يجوز للمولى أن يتزوجها ولو أعتقها المولى وعلى العبد دين مستغرق ثم وطئها فولدت عتقت بالاستيلاد وعليه العقر لها ويثبت نسب الولد منه عند أبي حنيفة لأن العتق توقف عنده على أن ينفذ عند تملك الجارية ألا ترى أنه لو قضى دين الغرماء أو أبرأ الغرماء العبد من ديونهم حتى ملك الجارية نفذ عتقه فكذا إذا ملك الجارية بالاستيلاد. ولو تزوج جارية عبده المأذون المديون لا يجوز؛ ذكره في المحيط. وذكر المولى مثال فإن العبد المأذون المديون إذا باعه المولى من غير إذن الغرماء وأعتقه المشتري قبل قبضه ينفذ عتقه إن أجاز الغرماء البيع أو قضى المولى دين الغرماء، وإن أبرأ الغرماء العبد عن الدين ينفذ عتق المشتري، فإن أبى الغرماء أن يجيزوا البيع والمولى لم يقض دينه فإنه يبطل عتقه ويباع العبد للغرماء بدينهم هكذا ذكر في الأصل مطلقاً. وهذا الجواب الذي قالوا لا يشكل على قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، أما على قول محمد رحمه الله تعالى فمنهم من قال لا يقف عتق المشتري على قول محمد، ومنهم من قال ما ذكر قولهم جميعاً وعلى قول محمد يحتاج إلى الفرق هذا وبين المشتري من الغاصب وهذا إذا أعتق المشتري قبل القبل، وأما إذا قبض العبد بين ثم أعتقه فإنه ينفذ عتقه، وإذا تقدم عتق المشتري بعد القبض فالغرماء بعد هذا بالخيار إن شاءوا أجاز البيع وأخذوا الثمن، وإن شاءوا ضمنوه القيمة هذا إذا أجازوا بيع المولى، وإن ضمنوا قيمته للمولى فبيع المولى ينفذ ويسلم الثمن للمولى ولو كان المشتري باع العبد بعد ما قبضه أو وهبه وقبضه الموهوب له ثم حضر الغرماء وأجازوا بيع المولى ينفذ بيع المشتري وهبته من غيره. ولو قال المؤلف فيتوقف تحريره لكان أولى لأن غايته تصرف فضولي. وقد أفاد في المحيط في مسألة الأمة المستولدة أنه موقوف فالعتق كذلك. قال رحمه الله: (وإن لم يحط صح) يعني وإن لم يحط الدين برقبته وبما في يده جاز عتقه وهذا بالإجماع، أما عندهما فظاهر وكذا عنده في قوله الآخر، وفي قوله الأول لا يملك فلا إعتاقه لأن الدين يتعلق يصح بكسبه وفي حق التعلق لا فرق بين القليل والكثير كما في الرهن. ووجه قول الآخر أن الفراغ وبعضه فارغ وبعضه مشغول فلا يجوز أن: الملك الحال لأن شرط يمنع في الملك لم يوجد ولا يجوز أن يمنع بقدره لأن البعض ليس بأولى من البعض الآخر؛ كذا نقله الشارح. وفي الهداية: وإن لم يكن محيطاً بماله جاز عتقه ولم يذكر رقبته وهذا هو القسم الأقسام التي ذكرناها قال في العناية: وإذا لم يكن محيطاً بماله ورقبته جاز عتق من المولى عبداً من كسبه. قال في بيوع الجامع الصغير عن يعقوب في رجل أذن لعبده في التجارة فاشترى عبداً يساوي ألفاً وعلى الأول ألف دين فأعتق المولى العبد المشتري فعتقه جائز، وإن كان الدين ألفي درهم مثل قيمته لم يجز عتقه ا.هـ. ولا يخفى أن إنفاذ العتق على قول الإمام فيما لو أحاط بكسبه إشكال لأن حاصل مذهبه أنه ملك المولى بطريق الخلافة عند الفراغ وهذا ليس بفارغ فظهر أن ذكر الرقبة لا فائدة فيه وأن المراد بالصحة النفاذ.
Book of the Authorized (Slave): From his earnings, and if it does not encompass, it is valid, and his sale to the master is not valid except for like value. And if the master sells from him, and if he (the master) causes a slave woman of his authorized slave, who has debt encompassing (his assets), to become umm walad, she becomes umm walad for him, and he guarantees her value, and he does not guarantee her offspring nor the value of her child. This is by agreement because according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) his ownership is established in reality, and according to him (Abu Hanifa) it coincides with the right of ownership. Hence it is permissible for the master to marry her. And if the master emancipates her while the slave has encompassing debt, then he (the master) has intercourse with her and she gives birth, she is emancipated by istilad, and upon him is the 'aqr for her, and the lineage of the child is established from him according to Abu Hanifa because emancipation, according to him, is suspended on being executed when he owns the slave woman. Do you not see that if he paid the debt of the creditors or the creditors released the slave from their debts until he owned the slave woman, his emancipation would be executed? Likewise if he owns the slave woman by istilad. And if he marries the slave woman of his authorized indebted slave, it is not permissible; mentioned in al-Muhit. And the master gives an example: if the authorized indebted slave is sold by the master without the permission of the creditors, and the buyer emancipates him before taking possession, his emancipation is executed if the creditors approve the sale or the master pays the debt of the creditors. And if the creditors release the slave from the debt, the buyer's emancipation is executed. If the creditors refuse to approve the sale and the master does not pay his debt, then his emancipation is void and the slave is sold for the creditors for their debt. Thus it is mentioned in al-Asl absolutely. This answer that they said is not problematic according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; as for the saying of Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, some said: the buyer's emancipation is not suspended according to Muhammad, and some said: what was mentioned is the saying of all of them, and according to Muhammad, a distinction is needed between this and between the buyer from the usurper. And this is if the buyer emancipates before possession; but if he takes possession of the slave between then and then emancipates him, then his emancipation is executed. And if the buyer's emancipation occurs after possession, the creditors after this have the choice: if they wish, they approve the sale and take the price; if they wish, they make him liable for the value. This is if they approve the master's sale. And if they make him liable for its value to the master, then the master's sale is executed and the price goes to the master. And if the buyer sold the slave after he had taken possession, or gifted him and the donee took possession, then the creditors come and approve the master's sale, the buyer's sale and gift from others is executed. And if the author had said 'it is suspended', its editing would have been better because its ultimate is a disposition of a non-owner. And it is stated in al-Muhit in the issue of the umm walad slave woman that it is suspended; likewise emancipation. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if it does not encompass, it is valid) meaning if the debt does not encompass his person and what is in his hand, his emancipation is valid, and this is by consensus. As for according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is apparent; likewise according to him (Abu Hanifa) in his other saying. In his first saying, he does not own, so no emancipation, because debt attaches to his earnings, and in respect of attachment, there is no difference between little and much, as in the case of a pledge. And the face of the other saying is that the vacant (portion) and some of it is vacant and some of it occupied, so it is not permissible that: the present ownership because a condition preventing ownership did not exist, nor is it permissible to prevent by its measure because some is not more deserving than some other; thus the commentator transmitted it. And in al-Hidaya: And if it is not encompassing his wealth, his emancipation is valid, and he did not mention his person; this is one of the divisions we mentioned. He said in al-Inayah: And if it is not encompassing his wealth and his person, the emancipation by the master of a slave from his earnings is valid. He said in the Sales of al-Jami' al-Saghir from Ya'qub: concerning a man who authorized his slave for trade, so he bought a slave worth one thousand and upon the first (slave) was a debt of one thousand dinars, then the master emancipated the purchased slave, his emancipation is valid. And if the debt was two thousand dirhams equal to his value, his emancipation is not valid. End. And it is not hidden that the execution of emancipation according to the Imam in the case where it encompasses his earnings is problematic because the gist of his madhhab is that he owns the master by way of deputyship at the time of vacancy, and this is not vacant. So it becomes apparent that mentioning the person has no benefit and that by validity is meant execution.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of the authorized slave's emancipation when his earnings are not entirely consumed by debt. The author first presents the basic ruling: if the debt does not encompass the slave's earnings (kash), the emancipation is valid. If it does encompass, the ruling differs. The commentary then discusses the istilad case (producing offspring with the master) and the sale of the slave by the master when he is in debt, with examples and intra-Hanafi disagreements. The key dispute is between Abu Hanifa's earlier and later positions regarding the slave's ownership of his earnings. Abu Hanifa's first position holds that the slave owns nothing; thus emancipation is invalid if debt encompasses. His later position, along with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, holds that the slave can own, so emancipation is valid as long as the debt does not fully encumber his person and earnings. The commentary also clarifies the distinction between 'sahih' (valid) and 'nafidh' (executed) in this context, concluding that here validity means execution (nufadh). The author cites various sources (al-Muhit, al-Hidaya, al-Inaya, al-Jami' al-Saghir) to support the reasoning.

Key Terms
المأذون (al-ma'dhun): A slave who has been given permission to trade.
محاطة الدين (muhatah al-dayn): Debt that fully covers the slave's assets (person and earnings).
الاستيلاد (al-istilad): Master causing his slave woman to give birth to his child, making her umm walad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the text, when is the emancipation of an authorized slave valid?
A) Only if the slave has no debt whatsoever.
B) If the debt does not encompass the slave's person and earnings.
C) If the master pays all the slave's debts first.
D) It is never valid because the slave cannot own.

Key Takeaway
The key is that the slave's partial ownership allows valid emancipation provided debt does not fully encumber his person and earnings.

Suspension of Buyer's Emancipation and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Creditor Consent
Commentary on buyer's emancipation and creditor consent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling on a buyer's emancipation of an authorized indebted slave when the sale was made without creditor consent, and distinguish between the views of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on suspension.

Core Idea
The buyer's emancipation is suspended on creditor consent; Muhammad's view requires a distinction from the usurper case.

This lesson continues from the previous one, examining a practical scenario: the master sells his indebted authorized slave without the creditors' permission, and the buyer emancipates the slave. The text presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the emancipation is suspended or not, and the conditions for its execution. Understanding this helps in applying correct fatwa in transactional slavery cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and initial ruling
The scenario: master sells indebted authorized slave to a buyer without creditor permission. The buyer emancipates before taking possession. The text gives a series of outcomes based on creditor actions.
Focus on the ruling that if creditors refuse and master doesn't pay, emancipation is void.
2
Locate the dispute on suspension
The text says 'لا يشكل على قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف' then mentions that according to Muhammad, some scholars deny suspension, some affirm it but require a distinction. Identify the point of disagreement: whether the buyer's emancipation is suspended (tawaquf) or not.
Muhammad's view is less clear; the text suggests need for distinction.
3
Analyse the distinction with the usurper case
The text hints that Muhammad's view requires distinguishing between a buyer from a non-owner (usurper) and a buyer from the master (owner). In the usurper case, the buyer's emancipation might not be suspended; here it might be. Understand the basis: the master's ownership is valid, but subject to creditors' rights.
4
Apply the thamarah
The practical consequence: if the emancipation is not suspended (according to some interpretations of Muhammad), then the buyer's emancipation takes effect immediately, and creditors can only claim the price or value. If it is suspended, it only takes effect if creditors consent or master pays debt.

كتاب المأذون من كسبه وإن لم يحط صح ولم يصح بيعه من السيد إلا بمثل القيمة وإن باع سيده منه ولو استولد جارية عبده المأذون له وعليه دين مستغرق وصارت أم ولد له ويضمن قيمتها ولا يضمن عرقها ولا قيمة ولدها ضمنوه القيمة هذا إذا أجازوا بيع المولى، وإن ضمنوا قيمته للمولى فبيع المولى ينفذ ويسلم الثمن للمولى ولو كان المشتري باع العبد بعد ما قبضه أو وهبه وقبضه الموهوب له ثم حضر الغرماء وأجازوا بيع المولى ينفذ بيع المشتري وهبته من غيره. ولو قال المؤلف فيتوقف تحريره لكان أولى لأن غايته تصرف فضولي. وقد أفاد في المحيط في مسألة الأمة المستولدة أنه موقوف فالعتق كذلك. قال رحمه الله: (وإن لم يحط صح) يعني وإن لم يحط الدين برقبته وبما في يده جاز عتقه وهذا بالإجماع، أما عندهما فظاهر وكذا عنده في قوله الآخر، وفي قوله الأول لا يملك فلا إعتاقه لأن الدين يتعلق يصح بكسبه وفي حق التعلق لا فرق بين القليل والكثير كما الهداية: وإن لم يكن محيطاً بماله جاز عتقه ولم يذكر رقبته وهذا هو القسم الأقسام التي ذكرناها قال في العناية: وإذا لم يكن محيطاً بماله ورقبته جاز عتق من المولى عبداً من كسبه. قال في بيوع الجامع الصغير عن يعقوب في رجل أذن لعبده في التجارة فاشترى عبداً يساوي ألفاً وعلى الأول ألف دين فأعتق المولى العبد المشتري فعتقه جائز، وإن كان الدين ألفي درهم مثل قيمته لم يجز عتقه ا.هـ. ولا يخفى أن إنفاذ العتق على Book of the Authorized (Slave): From his earnings, and if it does not encompass, it is valid, and his sale to the master is not valid except for like value. And if the master sells from him, and if he (the master) causes a slave woman of his authorized slave, who has debt encompassing (his assets), to become umm walad, she becomes umm walad for him, and he guarantees her value, and he does not guarantee her offspring nor the value of her child. This is by agreement because according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) his ownership is established in reality, and according to him (Abu Hanifa) it coincides with the right of ownership. Hence it is permissible for the master to marry her. And if the master emancipates her while the slave has encompassing debt, then he (the master) has intercourse with her and she gives birth, she is emancipated by istilad, and upon him is the 'aqr for her, and the lineage of the child is established from him according to Abu Hanifa because emancipation, according to him, is suspended on being executed when he owns the slave woman. Do you not see that if he paid the debt of the creditors or the creditors released the slave from their debts until he owned the slave woman, his emancipation would be executed? Likewise if he owns the slave woman by istilad. And if he marries the slave woman of his authorized indebted slave, it is not permissible; mentioned in al-Muhit. And the master gives an example: if the authorized indebted slave is sold by the master without the permission of the creditors, and the buyer emancipates him before taking possession, his emancipation is executed if the creditors approve the sale or the master pays the debt of the creditors. And if the creditors release the slave from the debt, the buyer's emancipation is executed. If the creditors refuse to approve the sale and the master does not pay his debt, then his emancipation is void and the slave is sold for the creditors for their debt. Thus it is mentioned in al-Asl absolutely. This answer that they said is not problematic according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; as for the saying of Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, some said: the buyer's emancipation is not suspended according to Muhammad, and some said: what was mentioned is the saying of all of them, and according to Muhammad, a distinction is needed between this and between the buyer from the usurper. And this is if the buyer emancipates before possession; but if he takes possession of the slave between then and then emancipates him, then his emancipation is executed. And if the buyer's emancipation occurs after possession, the creditors after this have the choice: if they wish, they approve the sale and take the price; if they wish, they make him liable for the value. This is if they approve the master's sale. And if they make him liable for its value to the master, then the master's sale is executed and the price goes to the master. And if the buyer sold the slave after he had taken possession, or gifted him and the donee took possession, then the creditors come and approve the master's sale, the buyer's sale and gift from others is executed. And if the author had said 'it is suspended', its editing would have been better because its ultimate is a disposition of a non-owner. And it is stated in al-Muhit in the issue of the umm walad slave woman that it is suspended; likewise emancipation. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if it does not encompass, it is valid) meaning if the debt does not encompass his person and what is in his hand, his emancipation is valid, and this is by consensus. As for according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is apparent; likewise according to him (Abu Hanifa) in his other saying. In his first saying, he does not own, so no emancipation, because debt attaches to his earnings, and in respect of attachment, there is no difference between little and much, as in the case of a pledge. And the face of the other saying is that the vacant (portion) and some of it is vacant and some of it occupied, so it is not permissible that: the present ownership because a condition preventing ownership did not exist, nor is it permissible to prevent by its measure because some is not more deserving than some other; thus the commentator transmitted it. And in al-Hidaya: And if it is not encompassing his wealth, his emancipation is valid, and he did not mention his person; this is one of the divisions we mentioned. He said in al-Inayah: And if it is not encompassing his wealth and his person, the emancipation by the master of a slave from his earnings is valid. He said in the Sales of al-Jami' al-Saghir from Ya'qub: concerning a man who authorized his slave for trade, so he bought a slave worth one thousand and upon the first (slave) was a debt of one thousand dinars, then the master emancipated the purchased slave, his emancipation is valid. And if the debt was two thousand dirhams equal to his value, his emancipation is not valid. End. And it is not hidden that the execution of emancipation according to the Imam in the case where it encompasses his earnings is problematic because the gist of his madhhab is that he owns the master by way of deputyship at the time of vacancy, and this is not vacant. So it becomes apparent that mentioning the person has no benefit and that by validity is meant execution.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of the authorized slave's emancipation when his earnings are not entirely consumed by debt. The author first presents the basic ruling: if the debt does not encompass the slave's earnings (kash), the emancipation is valid. If it does encompass, the ruling differs. The commentary then discusses the istilad case (producing offspring with the master) and the sale of the slave by the master when he is in debt, with examples and intra-Hanafi disagreements. The key dispute is between Abu Hanifa's earlier and later positions regarding the slave's ownership of his earnings. Abu Hanifa's first position holds that the slave owns nothing; thus emancipation is invalid if debt encompasses. His later position, along with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, holds that the slave can own, so emancipation is valid as long as the debt does not fully encumber his person and earnings. The commentary also clarifies the distinction between 'sahih' (valid) and 'nafidh' (executed) in this context, concluding that here validity means execution (nufadh). The author cites various sources (al-Muhit, al-Hidaya, al-Inaya, al-Jami' al-Saghir) to support the reasoning.

Key Terms
التصرف الفضولي (al-tasarruf al-fuduli): A disposition made without authority by a non-owner, which is suspended on ratification by the owner.
التوقف (al-tawaquf): Suspension; the ruling depends on a future condition (creditor consent or master payment).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what happens if the buyer emancipates the authorized slave before taking possession and the creditors refuse to approve the sale and the master does not pay the debt?
A) The emancipation is executed and the buyer must compensate the creditors.
B) The emancipation is void and the slave is sold for the creditors.
C) The emancipation is suspended indefinitely.
D) The emancipation is valid but the master must pay compensation.

Key Takeaway
The buyer's emancipation of an indebted authorized slave is suspended on creditor consent; without it, the emancipation is void.

Authorized Slave Selling to Master at a Discount: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining the validity of sale when the authorized slave sells to his master at less than market price.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the validity of an authorized slave's sale to his master at a discount, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of their disagreement.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa voids any discount sale to the master; the Sahibayn allow it with an option to remedy.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: when an authorized slave sells his merchandise to his own master at a price below market value, is the sale valid? The text presents the views of Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and explores the underlying rationale related to creditors' rights and the extent of permissible discount. Understanding this dispute reveals the Hanafi school's internal flexibility in balancing contractual freedom with protection of third-party rights.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's position
Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling: the sale is not valid unless the price equals the market value exactly. Any discount, whether large or small, renders the sale void because of suspicion (tuhmah) and harm to creditors' rights.
This is the default ruling in the matn.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the sale is valid even with a discount, but the master is given the choice (khiyar) to either remove the loss (pay the difference) or annul the sale.
They focus on the possibility of remedying the harm rather than voiding the contract outright.
3
Follow the proof for each view
Abu Hanifa's proof: creditors' rights attach to the exact value; any discount invalidates their right. The Sahibayn's proof: the discount can be compensated, so the sale stands with the option to rectify.
The underlying 'illa is the presence or absence of irretrievable harm to creditors.
4
Analyze the nuance of taghabun
The text introduces the concept of 'taghabun' (customary discount) especially in the context of the master's illness. Abu Hanifa uses a fixed fraction (one-third); the Sahibayn refer to what is customary. This affects the remedy.
This nuance is relevant when the master is sick and the sale is suspected of harming heirs.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, the sale is batil (void) from the outset, so no rescission is possible. Under the Sahibayn, the sale is valid and binding unless the master exercises his option to annul or compensate.
The practical difference: one leads to automatic invalidity, the other to a conditional valid sale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والصحة قال رحمه الله: (ولم يصح بيعه من السيد إلا بمثل القيمة) لأنه لا تهمة في البيع بمثل القيمة فيجوز وبأقل منه فيه تهمة فلا يجوز سواء كان النقصان كثيراً أو قليلاً. والمراد بعدم النفاذ لأجل الغرماء لأن حق الغرماء تعلق بالمالية فليس له أن يبطل حقهم. وقيد بالسيد لأنه لو حابا الأجنبي عند الإمام جاز لأنه لا تهمة فيه، وبخلاف ما لو باع المريض عيناً من وارثه بمثل القيمة حيث لا يجز عند الإمام لأن المريض ممنوع من إيثار بعض الورثة بها وفي حق غيرهم ممنوع عن إبطال المالية حتى كان له أن ماله يبيع جميع بمثل من القيمة وبأقل منه إلى ثلثي القيمة إذا لم يكن عليه دين وهذا عند الإمام. وعندهما إن باع من المولى جاز فاحشاً كان الغبن أو يسراً، ولكن يخير بين أن يزيل الغبن أو ينقض البيع لأن في المحاباة إبطال حق الغرماء في المالية فيتضررون به بخلاف البيع من الأجنبي بالغبن اليسير حيث يجوز بخلاف ما إذا باع من الأجنبي بالكثير من المحاباة حيث لا يجوز أصلاً عندهما، ومن المولى يجوز ويؤمر بإزالة المحاباة ولا يجوز من العبد المأذون على أصلهما إلا بإذن المولى ولا إذن. وفي الكافي وإن باعه من المولى بنقصان لم يجز فاحشاً كان أو يسيراً ولكن يخير المولى بين أن يزيل الغبن أو ينقض البيع وهذا قول بعض مشايخنا. وقيل إن الصحيح أن قول الإمام في هذه كقولهما. وفي المحيط: قول الكل وقيل قولهما ولو استهلك المولى المبيع في هذه الحالة لزمه تمام القيمة. وفي التتارخانية: برقم ومما يتصل بهذا الفصل: إذا باع العبد المأذون بعض ما في يده من تجارة أو اشترى شيئاً ببعض المال تجارة وحابا في ذلك وكان ذلك في مرض المولى ثم مات المولى من مرضه ذلك فعلى قول أبي حنيفة البيع جائز سواء حايا في البيع بما يتغابن الناس من مثله أو لا ما لم تجاوز المحاباة ثلث مال المولى، فإذا جاوز ثلث مال المولى فإنه يخير المشتري وإن شاء نقض البيع ولم يرد ما زاد على الثلث بخلاف ما لو كان المولى صحيحاً وحابا العبد بما يتغابن في مثله أو يتغابن الناس في مثله فإنه يجوز عند أبي حنيفة كيفما كان جاوزت المحاباة ثلث المال أم لم تجاوز، وهذا بخلاف المكاتب إذا باع أو اشترى وحابا في مرض موت المولى فإنه يجوز إذا لم تجاوز ثلث ماله فكذا العبد وهذا الذي ذكرنا كله قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى. وأما على قول أبي يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله تعالى إن باع واشترى بما يتغابن الناس من مثله فإنه يجوز ويسلم المشتري، ولو باع واشترى وحابا بما لا يتغابن الناس فيه لا يجوز البيع عندهما حتى إذا قال المشتري أنا أؤدي قدر المحاباة ولا ينقض البيع لا يكون له ذلك على قولهما. هذا الذي ذكرنا إذا لم يكن على العبد دين فأما إذا كان عليه دين يحيط برقبة
And validity: He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And his sale to the master is not valid except for like value) because there is no suspicion in the sale for like value, so it is permissible, and with less than it there is suspicion, so it is not permissible, whether the deficiency is much or little. And what is meant by non-execution is for the sake of the creditors, because the right of the creditors attaches to the value, so he may not invalidate their right. And it is restricted to the master because if he gives a discount to a stranger, according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa), it is permissible because there is no suspicion in it. Unlike if a sick person sells an item to his heir for like value, where it is not permissible according to the Imam because the sick person is prevented from favoring some heirs over others, and regarding others, he is prevented from invalidating the value, so that he may sell all his property for like value and for less up to two-thirds of the value if he has no debt; this according to the Imam. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if he sells to the master, it is permissible whether the loss is excessive or slight, but he is given the choice between removing the loss or annulling the sale, because in the discount there is invalidation of the creditors' right to value, so they are harmed by it. Unlike the sale to a stranger with slight loss, where it is permissible. Unlike if he sells to a stranger with much discount, where it is not permissible at all according to them. And from the master, it is permissible and he is ordered to remove the discount, and it is not permissible from the authorized slave according to their principle without the master's permission, and there is no permission. And in al-Kafi: And if he sold it to the master with a discount, it is not permissible, whether excessive or slight, but the master is given the choice between removing the loss or annulling the sale; this is the saying of some of our shaykhs. And it is said that the correct view is that the Imam's saying in this is like their saying. And in al-Muhit: The saying of all, and it is said their saying. And if the master consumed the sold item in this case, he is liable for the full value. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: By number, and related to this chapter: If the authorized slave sells some of what is in his hand from trade, or buys something with some of the trade capital, and gives a discount in that, and that is during the illness of the master, then the master dies from that illness, then according to Abu Hanifa, the sale is permissible whether he gave a discount in the sale by what people usually overlook or not, as long as the discount does not exceed one-third of the master's wealth. If it exceeds one-third of the master's wealth, then the buyer has the choice: if he wishes, he annuls the sale and does not return what exceeds the third. Unlike if the master was healthy and the slave gave a discount by what is usually overlooked or what people usually overlook, then it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa however it is, whether the discount exceeded a third of the wealth or not. And this is unlike the mukatib if he sells or buys and gives a discount during the illness of the master's death, then it is permissible if it does not exceed one-third of his wealth; likewise the slave. All this that we mentioned is the saying of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. As for according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, if he sells and buys by what people usually overlook, then it is permissible and the buyer is safe. And if he sells and buys and gives a discount by what people do not usually overlook, the sale is not permissible according to them. Even if the buyer says 'I will pay the amount of the discount and not annul the sale', he does not have that according to their saying. This that we mentioned is if the slave has no debt; but if he has debt that encompasses his person...
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling when an authorized slave sells his merchandise to his own master at a price below market value (muhabah). The base matn states that such a sale is not valid unless the price equals the market value. The commentary explains that this is because the slave's assets are encumbered by the rights of creditors (if any), and selling at a discount would harm them. The ruling is restricted to the master because selling at a discount to a stranger is permissible according to Abu Hanifa. The text then details the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa distinguishes between selling to the master (invalid unless at market price) and selling to a stranger (valid even with moderate discount). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow the sale to the master even with discount, but give the master the option to either remove the loss or annul the contract. Further discussion covers cases where the master is ill, comparing with rules of bequest to heirs, and the difference between the authorized slave and a mukatib. The passage concludes by noting that if the slave has no debt, the rules may differ. The overriding concern is the protection of creditors' rights.

Key Terms
محاباة (muhabah): Selling at a price lower than market value; a discount given by the seller.
تغابن (taghabun): The usual amount of price variation that people overlook in transactions; customary discount.
الغرماء (al-ghurama'): Creditors; those to whom the slave or master owes debts, whose rights attach to the assets.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), when an authorized slave sells to his master at a discount, the master has what option?
A) No option; the sale is void.
B) The option to remove the loss or annul the sale.
C) The option to return the slave.
D) The option to pay the slave less than market value.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on this issue turns on whether the discount to the master is treated as suspicious per se (Abu Hanifa) or remediable (Sahibayn), with later Fuqaha offering tarjih to the latter.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
advanced
15 min
Sale with Concession: Master vs. Stranger
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sale with concession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a permitted slave's sale with concession to his master versus to a stranger, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding suspicion and creditors' rights.

Core Idea
A permitted slave cannot sell to his master at a discount because it harms creditors; selling to a stranger at a small concession is allowed.

The permitted slave (al-madhun) has the capacity to trade, but his transactions are subject to the rights of creditors and the master's ownership. Selling at a discount (muhabah) raises suspicion (tuhma) of collusion, especially when the buyer is the master. This lesson examines the core dispute between the founders of the Hanafi school on the validity of such sales.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Parties
The act is the sale of an item by a permitted slave at a price below market value (muhabah). The buyer is either the master (al-sayyid) or a stranger (ajnabi). Determine which scenario is being analyzed.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, sale to the master is invalid (batil) regardless of the size of the concession because of the suspicion of harming creditors. Sale to a stranger is valid if the concession is not excessive (within what people overlook).
Abu Hanifa's focus is on the tuhma that the master is benefiting unjustly at the expense of creditors.
3
State the Sahibayn's Position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that sale to the master is valid but the master has the choice (takhyir) to either pay the difference or rescind the sale. Sale to a stranger with a large concession (fahish) is invalid, but with a small concession it is valid.
The Sahibayn allow the sale with a remedy, whereas Abu Hanifa blocks it outright.
4
Identify the Underlying Principle
Both positions are based on protecting creditors' rights (huquq al-ghurama') and avoiding suspicion. The difference lies in whether the sale can be salvaged through compensation or is inherently flawed.
This is a case of qiyas khafi: the illah (effective cause) is the potential harm to creditors, but the two sides differ on how that harm is assessed and remedied.

It is not hidden that the execution of manumission according to Imam Abu Hanifa in the case where the debt encompasses his earnings is problematic because the outcome of his madhhab is that he owns the master by way of succession when free, and this one is not free, so it appears that mentioning the neck has no benefit and that what is meant by validity is execution. And what is meant by non-execution is because of the creditors, for the right of the creditors is attached to the financial value, so he is not allowed to invalidate their right. And it is restricted to the master because if he made a concession to a stranger, according to Imam Abu Hanifa it is permissible because there is no suspicion in it, unlike if a sick person sold an asset to his heir at equivalent value where it is not permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa because the sick person is prevented from preferring some heirs over others, and with respect to others he is prevented from invalidating the financial value, so he may sell all for equivalent value or less up to two-thirds of the value if there is no debt on him, and this is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. According to the two companions, if he sells to the master it is permissible whether the loss is large or small, but he has the choice between removing the loss or rescinding the sale because in the concession there is an invalidation of the rights of the creditors in the financial value, so they are harmed by it, unlike sale to a stranger with a small loss where it is permissible, unlike if he sells to a stranger with a large concession where it is not permissible at all according to them, and from the master it is permissible and he is ordered to remove the concession, and it is not permissible from the permitted slave according to their principle without the permission of the master, and there is no permission.
